<Review>Thanks to a friend telling me about a Bristol Farms Grocery Store opening soon in Yorba Linda, and subsequently seeing Yelper, Nick H.'s review during soft opening, I learned about the Grand Opening of Bristol Farms today in Yorba Linda, CA.

I've been a Bristol Farms customer for over 30 years.  I was excited to hear about the Grand Opening for their newest store.

I arrived 10 minutes to 9 AM and waited with hundreds and hundreds of people in line for the doors to open at 9 AM as promised. We stood for over 40 minutes, it was not until after 9:30 that the line started moving.

The allure of a free canvas bag for the first 300 customers sounded great, but they gave tickets out to those folks who arrived bright and early BUT they failed to let the other hundreds and hundreds of people who were patiently waiting in line know NOT to wait in line but just proceed to enter and start shopping in the store.  Bristol, for future grand openings, please keep this in mind.  A lot of us felt our time was wasted and or just left and went home.

I stayed, helped a 90 year old elderly lady into the store to avoid heat stroke from standing in line outside in the sun too long, and somehow managed to enjoy the store despite the overcrowding of customers.  I grabbed a bagel, cream cheese, and coffee and had a seat at their indoor dining area.

Samples, as always with Bristol Farms, were generous.  Since I was in between breakfast and lunch I visited other stores in the shopping center and waited for my husband to join me for lunch at Bristol.

We ordered a Banh Mi Sandwich made with 10 hour roasted Pork.  The flavors were not as stand out as I would have hoped for, I was disappointed in the flavors of the sandwich.  Not enough punch in the pickled veggies of the sandwich.

Although the store was staffed more than adequately, there was trouble ringing up coupons, etc. as some cashiers were still learning the system.

The best things about Bristol are: Produce, Meats, Cheese and THE COOKIE (like a double tree cookie on steroids).  Apparently for the next three weeks the're running some great store deals.  Also email sign ups provide coupons for free items, like the dozen eggs I got for free today.

For grocery stores, it is hard to beat Bristol Farms in quality of produce and food items, I just wished my sandwich tasted better!<//Review><Pics>None<//Pics>< resp>
None<//resp>

< Name>
Curt P< /Name>
<Date>1577418126953<//Date>< text>
Given that it's supposed to be the best place for dim sum in Oakland Chinatown, we arrived before noon on Monday to avoid the crowd.  The place is basic and  on the small side, not many tables, so folks were already waiting and more came to wait by 12:30pm.  We got a seat quickly because we agreed to share a large table with others.

Prices aren't high, but also not as low as you expect for the set up (basic, not fancy) and portion size (small to average).  Biggest downer was the "Shanghai dumpling" (which is supposed to be Xiao long bao, with soup on the inside) because it had no soup on the inside and might as well be sui mai.  The other downer was that the skin/shell of all the dim sum we ordered (we ordered 6 dishes) was consistently too soft/wet/mushy (it should be a little more firm).

We'll likely come back, mostly because it's walkable from our place and because we haven't found a better dim sum place in Oakland Chinatown.  It's just not good enough to visit more than  once a month.< /text>

< review>
I've eaten at Oso a million times at this point and it's one of the most consistent restaurants in Sonoma Valley! Not only does Chef Dave have a dedicated, friendly staff, but he's cultivated a cult of locals who love dining at the bar or on the patio (like me!).

My favorite dishes include hummus (with amazing bread), shrimp cocktail, ceviche, shrimp & grits, and seasonal salads.

They also are extremely accommodating. Vegetarian dishes can be made vegan, for example.

Also the bartenders are great. While Oso has a small wine list, it features a lot of small production, hyper local sustainable wines. They also have great cocktails - the Blood Orange Margarita is one of the best drinks in the region.

OSO also shares my same values of inclusivity, celebrating diversity, and supporting democratic values. These are all things I look for when I'm considering where I'd like to spend my hard earned money!< /review>

3.5 stars rounded up to 4. We had a pleasant date night at Oso.

We shared a bunch of small plates, like burrata, broccolini, and deviled eggs. They were somewhat hit or miss - the burrata was the star of the show, with a large, creamy portion complemented by ripe tomatoes and brightened by vinegar. The broccolini was good, not great. It was more like chopped florets than broccolini, but the chick peas and parm were a nice touch. The deviled eggs were huge, though mostly flavorless.

The ambiance and enough of the food was good that I'd come back!< /text>

<review>This superior restaurant and bar on the square in Sonoma, CA is a must visit.

I arrived during their Happy Hour (M-Th beginning at 5) and was greeted by the hostess, a server and the bartender, Rob. Talk about feeling welcome!

I selected a Syrah and decided to start with their Dungeness Crab Deviled Eggs. The house made yellow curry paste with a touch of paprika really made these a stand out.

Next up, I went for a fresh oyster tour. Two west coasters: Fanny Bay from British Columbia, A Capital Gen from WA, and the east coast New Brunswick Beausoleil. Tamari mignonette spiced nicely and topped with a jalape√±o slice floater along with what a sweet ketchup base cocktail sauce. All too notch-though not big-flavorful oysters.

My main course was one of the night's specials-a New York Strip Ramen!  A wonderfully rich full flavored broth! The noodles are cooked in the broth which is dark and hearty, an abundance of relatively thin sliced New York strip steak, sliced and quartered shiitake mushrooms, daikon radish greens and thinly sliced Easter radish round out this flavor champion dish.

You need to dine (and drink) at Oso! The staff, with their unobtrusive casual friendliness, compliment both the food and atmosphere. I will, without a doubt, dine here again!<//review><pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOrm2C2jE-o_Ba-e7aJxLfKWIwPsmf7RHis-hJc=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNq9r5Hxjil3QwRPA2bjKCgUSLbUMLMk4378LeC=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPMVMwNreS1fny9z8uz8Q9ob4rvVyl1Y4pIJHfC=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNJpnOK-TSqE5fDtujT_l6JCO0qLFB59Hpw36MC=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]< /pics><Resp>None</Resp><GmapID>0x8085aea804662a43:0xb791e1449d98dfeb<//GmapID></record></dataset><record>

< Text>
Chef David Bush is a genius! Who'd thought deviled eggs could taste so mind blowing? The whole night was on point. The service was great, Kudos to the amazing and energetic manager and our lovely waitress! The restaurant is kinda small, beautifully designed and very very clean. The kitchen is right there in front you so you can see the whole thing.

As for the food, it was amazing. the deviled egg, absolutely spectacular. The grilled bread and mushroom was very tasty. I would preferred the bread to be less hard, because it was hard to cut, but still it was great. The tacos and braised beef short rib were delicious. Every dish was really very tasty. The Sake Sangria was great too.

I wish there's an Oso in San Francisco!</Text>

First time having deep dish pizza in 10yrs.
Artichoke dip had a good-interesting flavour, slight hint of curry spice, and it was very cheesy.

<Resp>None<//Resp><Review>Good Chicago-style stuffed pizza. Awful service.

The chain got sold in late 2018, and service has really gone downhill, especially at this Palo Alto location.

They're generally slow and understaffed, and they sometimes don't bother answering the phone. They've gotten orders wrong, and today they somehow managed to serve the pizza I ordered to someone else and had to re-make it, wasting 30 minutes of my day. (They didn't even offer a free appetizer or something to tide me over -- a sign that they just don't care.)

I'm giving up on this location and switching to the one in Campbell. So far it's still mostly okay, though I don't know how long that will last. I suspect the new owners are trying to extract as much money as they can by cutting costs. (An employee told me that wages were cut drastically, and it looks like staffing has been cut too.)

Original review below:

Patxi's reminds me a lot of Carmen's, a stuffed pizza restaurant I loved when I lived in Chicago and Evanston. They have the authentic crust with a bit of corn meal in it, and a nice, chunky tomato sauce.

The stuffed pizza is the real deal: two layers of crust with the "toppings" in between and more cheese on top where it melts into the top crust.  My favorite is the "Matt Cain" - a stuffed pizza with sausage and pepperoni. They also have a nice casual atmosphere and a good selection of beers and sodas.</Review>< username>
Laura Werner< /username>

<rating>5</rating>< text>
Miguel is one of the reason I'm giving Patxi's 5 stars. I was there with my 2 toddlers and 2 other people as we were waiting for 3 more people to arrive. He was very quick to attend to us. Considerate to ask us how we wanted seating arrangements for the high chairs ( most places just put them at the ends of the tables). He was very patient with ALL of our questions and was very knowledgeable about everything on the menu which was Extremely helpful for a our vegan request and it was our first time there. He was honest about the wait time once we ordered. While we waited he brought out pizza dough for my boys to play with and they had alot of fun with it. Our food was ready sooner than the estimated time which was great. When the rest of our party came he was again very quick to attend to them and answer questions. Made sure we had enough plates came around to refill drinks and was attentive through out our dining experience. He was helpful, polite & very friendly. His customer service  deserved more tips than what I was able to give him & we are truly beyond satisfied with our experience here. The food was delicious and very much worth the wait! Macio was very welcoming and kind which added to our experience.<//text>

<Date>1515804921581< /Date><user_id>110572154067518663643< /user_id>< review>
Patxi's is a mainstay of Palo Alto. With Pizza My Heart on University and Delfina, also on Emerson, you have the trifecta of PA Pizza. Patxi's is best known for and specializes in deep dish Chicago style pizza and does it very well. (I'm from Chicago) Their regs and thin crust are also excellent, as are the salads etc.

While the San Carlos Patxi's is a better venue and bar, by far, the Palo Alto Patxi's delivers on the main course: pizza.

Great happy hour too, which most people sleep on.</review>

<Text>The four stars is because this place is usually very good. The kitchen seemed to be a bit overwhelmed on our last visit though.

Stay away from the appetizer of wings. The sauce is good, but they're clearly baked in a cooler oven than you should use for that. The skin was rubbery and kind of gross.

We also got presented a wrong pie, noticed, and were able to mention it to our server  (who was super sweet, but completely swamped) before she served the first slices and then were served a different, also wrong pizza. Unfortunately, we didn't notice that it was wrong until we'd begun eating.

Because it's Paxti's, the pizza was delicious, even if it wasn't what we'd asked for, so we had the bill adjusted to reflect what we got.< /Text><Pics>None<//Pics>< Resp>

Maybe my fault for ordering sausage+pepperoni, but we thought the pie was on the salt-heavy side. <Rating>5<//Rating><text>For a long time we have been trying to find a good Chicago style deep dish pizza place in the Bay Area. As one of my friends highly recommended Patxi's, we decided to give it a shot on a Friday evening.

As parking is on the streets, we found a parking lot a couple of blocks away from this restaurant and walked here. No complaints; was definitely nice strolling the frenzied Palo Alto downtown.

Unfortunately, Patxi's does not accept reservations and we had a 45min wait time. However, they recommend pre-ordering pizzas given that there is 30-40min preparation time. They offer different styles of pizza; we chose the "Chicago Stuffed" pizza style to satiate our cravings and pre-ordered the 10" BBQ chicken combo.

The ambience was trendy; definitely a far cry from other pizzas places that offer a sportsbar atmosphere. Clearly, it not a conventional pizza place, where one could quickly grab a bite to eat.

Soon, we were seated and served pizzas at our table. Service was fantastic. Pizzas were delish. Quantity was huge; two of us shared the 10" pizza and we could not finish it. Definitely worth the bucks.

We loved it; Will certainly return to try more from their menu.< /text>< Pics>
